                        cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">New Insights into the Roles of Mg in Improving the Rate Capability and Cycling Stability of O3-NaMn0.48Ni0.2Fe0.3Mg0.02O2 for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Cheng; Gao, Rui; Zheng, Lirong; Hao, Yongmei; Liu, Xiangfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10819-10827</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Elements doping has been used to improve the electrochem. performances of O3-type layered transition metal oxide cathodes for sodium-ion batteries.  However, their roles and the improvement mechanism have not been clearly understood.  Herein, the effects of Mg substitution for Mn on the structure and electrochem. performances of NaMn0.48Ni0.2Fe0.3Mg0.02O2 have been comprehensively investigated and some new insights into the roles of Mg in improving the rate capability and cycling stability have been presented. (1) The substitution of Mg for Mn enlarges the interlayer spacing, which not only enhances Na+ diffusion and the rate capability but also alleviates the lattice strains induced by Na+ intercalation/deintercalation. (2) The substitution of Mg by Mn also shrinks TM-O bond and TMO2 slabs, which enhances the layered structure stability. (3) The Mg substitution also mitigates the structure distortion or vol. change of the crystal lattices and suppresses the irreversible phase transitions. (4) The substitution of low-valence Mg2+ for Mn3+ reduces Mn3+ and minimizes Jahn-Teller effect, which also further alleviates the irreversible phase transformations and improves the layered structure stability.  This study not only unveils the roles of Mg but also presents some insights into designing the cathode materials with both high rate capability and high cycling stability through the lattice structure regulation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoHcd3T9IZQ2bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgK53U_1a1cNQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXktlGiur4%253D&amp;md5=cb73f422a43a79020eedd776ee10e79a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2018.04.006"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z.-G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, T.-R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, X.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.-T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, B.-H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tuning the component ratio and corresponding sodium storage properties of layer-tunnel hybrid Na<sub>0.6</sub>Mn<sub>1-<i>x</i></sub>Ni<sub><i>x</i></sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode by a simple cationic Ni<sup>2+</sup> doping strategy</span>. <i>Electrochim. Acta</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>273</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">63</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2018.04.006</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D273%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D63%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DH.%2BChen%26author%3DZ.-G.%2BWu%26author%3DZ.%2BZheng%26author%3DT.-R.%2BChen%26author%3DX.-D.%2BGuo%26author%3DJ.-T.%2BLi%26author%3DB.-H.%2BZhong%26title%3DTuning%2Bthe%2Bcomponent%2Bratio%2Band%2Bcorresponding%2Bsodium%2Bstorage%2Bproperties%2Bof%2Blayer-tunnel%2Bhybrid%2BNa0.6Mn1-xNixO2%2Bcathode%2Bby%2Ba%2Bsimple%2Bcationic%2BNi2%252B%2Bdoping%2Bstrategy%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2018.04.006&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b07865&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2018.04.006&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tuning the component ratio and corresponding sodium storage properties of layer-tunnel hybrid Na0.6Mn1-xNixO2 cathode by a simple cationic Ni2+ doping strategy</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Hui; Wu, Zhenguo; Zheng, Zhuo; Chen, Tingru; Guo, Xiaodong; Li, Juntao; Zhong, Benhe</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">273</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">63-70</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Manganese (Mn)-based cathodes with advantages of low-cost, environmental benign, high energy d. are crucial for the com. process of sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  Layer-tunnel hybrid cathode, which aims to integrate high capacity of P2-type layered structure with excellent cycling stability, superior rate performance of tunnel structure, deserves great research efforts.  To further enhance the resp. performance, the ratio of layer-tunnel component in the hybrid Na0.6Mn1-xNixO2 was adjusted by a simple cationic Ni2+ doping route.  The crystal structure and electrochem. behavior of Na0.6Mn1-xNixO2 were carefully detected, compared and analyzed.  The comprehensive results evidenced that the layered component ratio would rapidly increase with Ni2+ doping.  The structural parameters of pure phase would also be affected by varied Ni2+ content.  And 5% Ni doping could be an optimized point in terms of reversible capacity, cycling stability, rate performance and reaction kinetics.  This study would reveal the dual-function of cationic doping in both macro scale component ratio and at. scale crystal lattice parameter, and grasp new insight into the design and optimization of high performance hybrid cathode for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqsszK1Ov_Z0rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgK53U_1a1cNQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXnsVenu7c%253D&amp;md5=e3e35305692682d5968e9a4288b6fc17</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2019.04.003"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, Y.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Boosting the reactivity of Ni2+/Ni3+ redox couple via fluorine doping of high performance Na0.6Mn0.95Ni0.05O2-xFx cathode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Hui; Wu, Zhenguo; Zhong, Yanjun; Chen, Tingru; Liu, Xiaohong; Qu, Jie; Xiang, Wei; Li, Juntao; Chen, Xianchun; Guo, Xiaodong; Zhong, Benhe</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">308</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Though P2-type Na-Mn-Ni-O cathodes with low cost and environmental benign were extensively studied, it is still challenging to fulfill practical application with limited cycle stability and low operating potential.  However, the research of the reactive Ni2+/Ni3+ redox pair that enable both high working potential and high reversible capacity was almost ignored.  And traditional cationic doping mainly focuses on crystal modulation and structure stabilization.  An anion doping strategy (F-doping) was carried out to further boost the activity of Ni2+.  The multi-function including structural parameter modulation and robust Ni-F bond significantly promote the activation of Ni2+/Ni3+ and advance the resp. working potential.  Related reaction kinetics and structural evolution were also studied to elucidate the F-doping mechanism.  The Na0.6Mn0.95Ni0.05O1.95F0.05 with appropriate F content could deliver a high capacity of 80.76 mA h g-1 at 2C with 75.0% retained after 960 cycles.  The excellent rate capability and full cell performance also demonstrate the high potential.  This study may provide a new sight for the development of P2-type layered Na-Mn-Ni-O cathode, which could be extended to other oxides cathode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGot0gv9FI-4SbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgK53U_1a1cNQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-Dimensional Chestnut-Like Architecture Assembled from NaTi3O6(OH)·2H2O@N-Doped Carbon Nanosheets with Enhanced Sodium Storage Properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Chunjin; Zhang, Zheng; Tang, Yi; Yang, Zuguang; Li, Yongchun; Zhong, Benhe; Wu, Zhen-guo; Guo, Xiaodong; Dou, Shi-xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The application of Na titanate anodes of low cost, feasible operating voltage, and nontoxic nature were severely hindered by their inferior cycling stability and poor rate capability.  Here, 3-dimensional (3D) chestnut-like NaTi3O6(OH)·2H2O@N-doped C nanospheres (NTOH@CN) with loose crystal structures were prepd. by a self-sacrificed template method.  The nanospheres were composed of nanosheets and linked with nanowires, which interweaved to construct a meshwork structure.  The growth mechanism of unique 3D NTOH@CN nanospheres was studied by tracking the synthesis process of different hydrothermal durations.  The rate performances of 3D NTOH@CN were superior to that of NaTi3O6(OH)·2H2O irregular spheres assembled from nanosheets (3D NTOH) and NaTi3O6(OH)·2H2O nanosheets (2-dimensional NTOH).  Excellent cycling and rate performance were obtained due to their open crystal structure, unique 3D nanosphere morphol. with short diffusion paths, N-doped C surrounding, and the solid soln. reaction.  The reaction mechanism, morphol. change, and dynamics research during the Na insertion/desertion process were studied.  Based on varying ex situ analyses, the irreversible metallic Ti formation and the excellent structural stability of nanosphere morphol. were evidenced.  The pseudocapacitive phenomenon was also detected, which effectively enhanced Na+ ion storage capability.  The systematical and comprehensive study provide a holograph for the design and synthesis of sodium titanate nanostructures.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRLjAnOqfsWLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZYw0RdiX_9w"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Design and Synthesis of Layered Na2Ti3O7 and Tunnel Na2Ti6O13 Hybrid Structures with Enhanced Electrochemical Behavior for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu Chunjin; Hua Weibo; Zhang Zheng; Zhong Benhe; Yang Zuguang; Feng Guilin; Xiang Wei; Wu Zhenguo; Guo Xiaodong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),

    </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel complementary approach for promising anode materials is proposed.  Sodium titanates with layered Na2Ti3O7 and tunnel Na2Ti6O13 hybrid structure are presented, fabricated, and characterized.  The hybrid sample exhibits excellent cycling stability and superior rate performance by the inhibition of layered phase transformation and synergetic effect.  The structural evolution, reaction mechanism, and reaction dynamics of hybrid electrodes during the sodium insertion/desertion process are carefully investigated.  In situ synchrotron X-ray powder diffraction (SXRD) characterization is performed and the result indicates that Na(+) inserts into tunnel structure with occurring solid solution reaction and intercalates into Na2Ti3O7 structure with appearing a phase transition in a low voltage.  The reaction dynamics reveals that sodium ion diffusion of tunnel Na2Ti6O13 is faster than that of layered Na2Ti3O7.  The synergetic complementary properties are significantly conductive to enhance electrochemical behavior of hybrid structure.  This study provides a promising candidate anode for advanced sodium ion batteries (SIBs).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcTOQT7xZP5J1DAEfvC7EH1LfW6udTcc2eZtS51v3nAEz7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In Operando Investigation of the Structural Evolution during Calcination and Corresponding Enhanced Performance of Three-Dimensional Na2Ti6O13@C-N Hierarchical Microflowers</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Chunjin; Shi, Chenguang; Yang, Lin; Zhang, Zheng; Tang, Yi; Yang, Zuguang; Yang, Ruikai; Wu, Zhen-guo; Guo, Xiaodong; Huang, Ling; Zhong, Benhe</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Industrial &amp; Engineering Chemistry Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">57</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">51</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Three-dimensional (3D) Na2Ti6O13 microflowers assembled from directionally arranged and closely interlinked one-dimensional N-doped carbon Na2Ti6O13 nanorods have been successfully prepd. by a self-sacrificed template method followed by sintering in argon.  In situ high-temp. X-ray powder diffraction (XRD) characterization was conducted to explore the phase transformation and structural evolution.  The results indicated that the NaTi3O6(OH)·2H2O precursor was converted into the tunnel Na2Ti6O13 phase and the layered Na2Ti3O7 phase at the different temps.  At a certain temp., the tunnel and layered phases have a mutual transformation.  The higher temp. was not conductive to the formation of pure phases.  The crystal structural evolution has been given based on the synthesis process and in situ high temp. XRD patterns.  When served as anode for SIBs, a capacity of ca. 30 mAh g-1 over 6000 continuous cycles was retained at 2000 mA g-1.                 10.1021/acs.chemrev.7b00007</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D117%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D13123%26journal%3DChem.%2BRev.%26author%3DF.%2BLin%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DX.%2BYu%26author%3DL.%2BCheng%26author%3DA.%2BSinger%26author%3DO.%2BG.%2BShpyrko%26author%3DH.-L.%2BXin%26author%3DN.%2BTamura%26author%3DC.%2BTian%26author%3DT.-C.%2BWeng%26author%3DX.-Q.%2BYang%26author%3DY.-S.%2BMeng%26author%3DD.%2BNordlund%26author%3DW.%2BYang%26author%3DM.-M.%2BDoeff%26title%3DSynchrotron%2BX-Ray%2BAnalytical%2BTechniques%2Bfor%2BStudying%2BMaterials%2BElectrochemistry%2Bin%2BRechargeable%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.chemrev.7b00007&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b07865&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.chemrev.7b00007&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synchrotron X-ray Analytical Techniques for Studying Materials Electrochemistry in Rechargeable Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lin, Feng; Liu, Yijin; Yu, Xiqian; Cheng, Lei; Singer, Andrej; Shpyrko, Oleg G.; Xin, Huolin L.; Tamura, Nobumichi; Tian, Chixia; Weng, Tsu-Chien; Yang, Xiao-Qing; Meng, Ying Shirley; Nordlund, Dennis; Yang, Wanli; Doeff, Marca M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Reviews (Washington, DC, United States)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">117</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13123-13186</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHREAY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0009-2665</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Rechargeable battery technologies have ignited major breakthroughs in contemporary society, including but not limited to revolutions in transportation, electronics, and grid energy storage.  The remarkable development of rechargeable batteries is largely attributed to in-depth efforts to improve battery electrode and electrolyte materials.  There are, however, still intimidating challenges of lower cost, longer cycle and calendar life, higher energy d., and better safety for large scale energy storage and vehicular applications.  Further progress with rechargeable batteries may require new chemistries (lithium ion batteries and beyond) and better understanding of materials electrochem. in the various battery technologies.  In the past decade, advancement of battery materials has been complemented by new anal. techniques that are capable of probing battery chemistries at various length and time scales.  Synchrotron X-ray techniques stand out as one of the most effective methods that allow for nearly nondestructive probing of materials characteristics such as electronic and geometric structures with various depth sensitivities through spectroscopy, scattering, and imaging capabilities.  This article begins with the discussion of various rechargeable batteries and assocd. important scientific questions in the field, followed by a review of synchrotron X-ray based anal. tools (scattering, spectroscopy, and imaging) and their successful applications (ex situ, in situ, and in operando) in gaining fundamental insights into these scientific questions.  Furthermore, electron microscopy and spectroscopy complement the detection length scales of synchrotron X-ray tools and are also discussed toward the end.  The importance is highlighted of studying battery materials by combining anal. techniques with complementary length sensitivities, such as the combination of X-ray absorption spectroscopy and electron spectroscopy with spatial resoln., because a sole technique may lead to biased and inaccurate conclusions.  The current progress is discussed of exptl. design for synchrotron expts. and methods to mitigate beam effects.  Finally, a perspective is provided to elaborate how synchrotron techniques can impact the development of next-generation battery chemistries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoHVtJqfZxyV7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZYw0RdiX_9w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsFOnu7rE&amp;md5=4ae0f00fac985f44b9e64177a70bb1aa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b09938"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Suppressing the Phase Transition of the Layered Ni-Rich Oxide Cathode during High-Voltage Cycling by Introducing Low-Content Li<sub>2</sub>MnO<sub>3</sub></span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Suppressing the Phase Transition of the Layered Ni-Rich Oxide Cathode during High-Voltage Cycling by Introducing Low-Content Li2MnO3</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Jun; Xia, Yongyao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The layered Ni-rich oxide cathode (LiNi0.8Co0.1Mn0.1O2) suffers from a tremendous structural degrdn. during high-voltage cycling (4.8 V), causing the drastic rise of electrode impedance and deterioration of the capacity retention.  Here, we develop an effective strategy to overcome these problems of the Ni-rich cathode material through doping low-content Li2MnO3 as an excellent structure stabilizer.  Cyclic voltammogram and ex-situ X-ray diffraction measurements have revealed that Li2MnO3 could display a remarkable suppression effect on the phase transition of LiNi0.8Co0.1Mn0.1O2.  The electrochem. tests showed that Li2MnO3-stabilized LiNi0.8Co0.1Mn0.1O2 could realize the large reversible capacity, stable discharge voltage and excellent cycling life during high-voltage cycling, which could be benefited from the enhanced structural stability of the modified Ni-rich cathode.  The Li2MnO3 could sufficiently suppress the phase transition between two hexagonal phase (H2 and H3) with distinctly different lattice parameters, significantly reducing variation of unit-cell vol., which facilitates stabilization of the original layered structure of LiNi0.8Co0.1Mn0.1O2 cathode during high-voltage cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqZIOV-qlUhbbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhRn6tRxa8IKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXitVygsLnI&amp;md5=51f9b753444c4eb2a36ab17d46ccafe3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1039/b108830k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Caballero, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hernan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Morales, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sanchez, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pena, J.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Aranda, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A layered sodium manganese oxide, Na0.6MnO2, stable at temps. &gt;800°, was synthesized by using a sol-gel method that employs Mn(acac)3 (ac = acetylacetonate), Na2CO3, and propionic acid to form the resin framework.  This layered bronze possesses a hexagonal, P2-type structure, in which the distortion assocd. with Mn3+ is hardly noticeable.  It reacts slowly, though reversibly, with atm. moisture, which causes the interlayer spacing in the structure to increase by ∼2.5 Å, by intercalation of water mols. into the interlayer gap occupied by Na+ ions.  The anhyd. material was tested as a cathode in sodium cells.  Although the electrochem. intercalation of Na+ occurs in two steps, the host retains its main structural features, with a slight tendency in the interlayer spacing to contract as the sodium content increases.  The similarity between the discharge and charge profiles of the first cycles reveals a quasi-reversible nature of the intercalation process and that the cell can deliver a const. sp. capacity of ∼140 A-h/kg at 0.1 mA/cm2 when cycled in a voltage region of 3.8-2.0 V.                 10.1021/acsami.7b11282</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D9%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D40215%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DX.%2BQi%26author%3DL.%2BLiu%26author%3DN.%2BSong%26author%3DF.%2BGao%26author%3DK.%2BYang%26author%3DY.%2BLu%26author%3DH.%2BYang%26author%3DY.-S.%2BHu%26author%3DZ.-H.%2BCheng%26author%3DL.%2BChen%26title%3DDesign%2Band%2BComparative%2BStudy%2Bof%2BO3%252FP2%2BHybrid%2BStructures%2Bfor%2BRoom%2BTemperature%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.7b11282&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b07865&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.7b11282&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Design and Comparative Study of O3/P2 Hybrid Structures for Room Temperature Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qi, Xingguo; Liu, Lilu; Song, Ningning; Gao, Fei; Yang, Kai; Lu, Yaxiang; Yang, Haitao; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Cheng, Zhao-Hua; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">46</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">40215-40223</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable sodium-ion batteries have drawn increasing attention as candidates for the post lithium-ion batteries in large-scale energy storage systems.  Layered oxides are the most promising cathode materials and their pure phases (e.g., P2, O3) have been widely investigated.  Here we report a series of cathode materials with O3/P2 hybrid phase for sodium-ion batteries, which possesses advantages of both P2 and O3 structures.  The designed material, Na0.78Ni0.2Fe0.38Mn0.42O2, can deliver a capacity of 86 mAh g-1 with great rate capability and cycling performance. 66% capacity is still maintained when the current rate reaches as high as 10C, and the capacity retention is 90% after 1500 cycles.  Moreover, in situ XRD was performed to examine the structure change during electrochem. testing in different voltage ranges, and the results demonstrate 4 V as the optimized upper voltage limit, with which smaller polarization, better structural stability, and better cycling performance are achieved.  The results obtained here provide new insights in designing cathode materials with optimal structure and improved performance for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpya-PJrurgV7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhRn6tRxa8IKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhslahu7rE&amp;md5=e6b74364f6ee9d10003fc84087c24f6c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA05205J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile Synthesis of Reduced Graphene Oxide Wrapped Nickel Silicate Hierarchical Hollow Spheres for Long-life Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Stable layered P3/P2 Na0.66Co0.5Mn0.5O2 cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Xiaoqing; Zhou, Xianlong; Hu, Meng; Liang, Jing; Wu, Dihua; Wei, Jinping; Zhou, Zhen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20708-20714</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable Na-ion batteries are promising next-generation energy storage devices due to the low cost and rich natural abundance of Na.  However, it is still a great challenge to suppress phase changes of cathode materials in the high-voltage region.  Unlike P-type single-phase composites, herein the authors present a facile strategy for prepg. P3/P2-type biphasic layered Na0.66Co0.5Mn0.5O2, namely, integrating P2 into P3-layered materials.  The cryst. structure of Na0.66Co0.5Mn0.5O2, which was studied by ex situ x-ray diffraction, was well maintained over long cycling in a high-voltage range.  Taking advantage of their structural stabilization, Na0.66Co0.5Mn0.5O2 cathode materials displayed remarkably steady discharge capacity at high rates.  With outstanding structural flexibility and electrochem. performance, Na0.66Co0.5Mn0.5O2 would stimulate the development of Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp37ddaxiNbTbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhRn6tRxa8IKA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mn-Based Cathode with Synergetic Layered-Tunnel Hybrid Structures and Their Enhanced Electrochemical Performance in Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Zhen-Guo; Li, Jun-Tao; Zhong, Yan-Jun; Guo, Xiao-Dong; Huang, Ling; Zhong, Ben-He; Agyeman, Daniel-Adjei; Lim, Jin-Myoung; Kim, Du-ho; Cho, Maeng-hyo; Kang, Yong-Mook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">25</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">21267-21275</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A synergistic approach for advanced cathode materials is proposed.  Sodium manganese oxide with a layered-tunnel hybrid structure was designed, synthesized, and subsequently investigated.  The layered-tunnel hybrid structure provides fast Na ion diffusivity and high structural stability thanks to the tunnel phase, enabling high rate capability and greatly improved cycling stability compared to that of the pure P2 layered phase while retaining the high specific capacity of the P2 layered phase.  The hybrid structure provided a decent discharge capacity of 133.4 mAh g-1 even at 8 C, which exceeds the reported best rate capability for Mn-based cathodes.  It also displayed an impressive cycling stability, maintaining 83.3 mAh g-1 after 700 cycles at 10 C.  Theor. calcn. and the potentiostatic intermittent titrn. technique (PITT) demonstrated that this hybrid structure helps enhance Na ion diffusivity during charge and discharge, attaining, as a result, an unprecendented electrochem. performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpZnDfNt6skELVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhoXSaY8YWAnA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Designing Air-Stable O3-Type Cathode Materials by Combined Structure Modulation for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yao, Hu-Rong; Wang, Peng-Fei; Gong, Yue; Zhang, Jienan; Yu, Xiqian; Gu, Lin; OuYang, Chuying; Yin, Ya-Xia; Hu, Enyuan; Yang, Xiao-Qing; Stavitski, Eli; Guo, Yu-Guo; Wan, Li-Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">139</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">25</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8440-8443</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As promising high-capacity cathode materials for Na-ion batteries, O3-type Na-based metal oxides (e.g., NaTMO2; TM = Co, Ni, Mn, Fe, etc.) always suffer from their poor air stability originating from the spontaneous extn. of Na and oxidn. of transition metals when exposed to air.  Herein, a combined structure modulation is proposed to tackle concurrently the two handicaps via reducing Na layers spacing and simultaneously increasing valence state of transition metals.  Guided by d. functional theory calcns., we demonstrate such a modulation can be subtly realized through Co-substitution of one kind of heteroatom with comparable electronegativity and another one with substantially different Fermi level, by adjusting the structure of NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 via Cu/Ti codoping.  The as-obtained NaNi0.45Cu0.05Mn0.4Ti0.1O2 exhibits an increase of 20 times in stable air-exposure period and 9 times in capacity retention after 500 cycles, and even retains its structure and capacity after being soaked in water.  Such a simple and effective structure modulation reveals a new avenue for high-performance O3-type cathodes and pushes the large-scale industrialization of Na-ion batteries a decisive step forward.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGobUgX2EF_-JrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhoXSaY8YWAnA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXpslSksr4%253D&amp;md5=f0a7d041b769c381f02a816a4e4b8332</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b00594"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, D.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.-P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.-X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Improved Electrochemical Performance of Fe-Substituted NaNi<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                 10.1021/acsami.5b00594</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D7%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D8585%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DD.-D.%2BYuan%26author%3DY.-X.%2BWang%26author%3DY.-L.%2BCao%26author%3DX.-P.%2BAi%26author%3DH.-X.%2BYang%26title%3DImproved%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BFe-Substituted%2BNaNi0.5Mn0.5O2%2BCathode%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.5b00594&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b07865&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.5b00594&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improved Electrochemical Performance of Fe-Substituted NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yuan, Ding D.; Wang, Yan X.; Cao, Yu L.; Ai, Xin P.; Yang, Han X.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">16</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8585-8591</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A series of O3-phase NaFex(Ni0.5Mn0.5)1-xO2 (x = 0, 0.1, 0.2, 0.3, 0.4, and 1) samples with different Fe contents was prepd. and investigated as high-capacity cathode materials of Na-ion batteries.  The partial substitution of Ni and Mn with Fe in the O3-phase lattice can greatly improve the electrochem. performance and the structural stability.  A NaFe0.2Mn0.4Ni0.4O2 cathode with an optimized Fe content of x = 0.2 can deliver an initial reversible capacity of 131 mA-h/g, a reversible capacity &gt;95% over 30 cycles, and a high rate capacity of 86 mA-h/g at 10C in a voltage range of 2.0-4.0 V.  The structural characterizations reveal that pristine NaMn0.5Ni0.5O2 and Fe-substituted NaFe0.2Mn0.4Ni0.4O2 lattices underwent different phase transformations from P3 to P3'' and from P3 to OP2 phases, resp., at high voltage interval.  The as-obtained OP2 phase by Fe substitution has smaller interslab distance (5.13 Å) than the P3'' phase (5.72 Å), which suppresses the co-insertion of the solvent mols., the electrolyte anions, or both and therefore enhances the cycling stability in the high voltage charge.  This finding suggests a new strategy for creating cycle-stable transition metal oxide cathodes for high-performance Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqmE18LkcOi57Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhoXSaY8YWAnA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cobalt-substituted Na0.44Mn1-xCoxO2: phase evolution and a high capacity positive electrode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Yu-Ting; Sun, Xin; Zou, Bang-Kun; Liao, Jia-Yin; Wen, Zhao-Yin; Chen, Chun-Hua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na0.44Mn1-xCoxO2 (x = 0, 0.01, 0.08, 0.11, 0.22, 0.33, 0.44) powders were synthesized as pos. electrodes for Na-ion batteries via a thermopolymn. method.  X-ray diffraction and SEM were used to analyze their crystal structures and particle morphologies.  Galvanostatic cell cycling was used to characterize the electrochem. properties.  The Co-substitution can change the structure of Na0.44Mn1-xCoxO2 from T-type (x = 0) into layered P2-type (x = 0.11) or P3-type (x = 0.44).  For the samples synthesized under the authors' specific conditions, the particle morphol. can be used as an indicator of their crystal structures: rod-like (T-type), plate-like (P2-type) and granules (P3-type).  P2-type Na0.44Mn0.89Co0.11O2 allows more Na+ intercalation into the inter-layer spacing and results in a high discharge capacity with 220 mAh g-1 at 12 mA g-1 in initial cycle, 180 mAh g-1 after 40 cycles in the voltage range of 2.0-4.2 V and a good rate performance of 104 mAh g-1 at a rate of 600 mA g-1 in the voltage range of 2.0-4.0 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoyoyb4o8UzULVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhoXSaY8YWAnA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cu2+ Dual-Doped Layer-Tunnel Hybrid Na0.6Mn1-xCuxO2 as a Cathode of Sodium-Ion Battery with Enhanced Structure Stability, Electrochemical Property, and Air Stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Ting-Ru; Sheng, Tian; Wu, Zhen-Guo; Li, Jun-Tao; Wang, En-Hui; Wu, Chun-Jin; Li, Hong-Tai; Guo, Xiao-Dong; Zhong, Ben-He; Huang, Ling; Sun, Shi-Gang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10147-10156</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been regarded as a promising candidate for large-scale renewable energy storage system.  Layered Mn oxide cathode possesses the advantages of high energy d., low cost and natural abundance while suffering from limited cycling life and poor rate capacity.  To overcome these weaknesses, layer-tunnel hybrid material was developed and served as the cathode of SIB, which integrated high capacity, superior cycle ability, and rate performance.  Here, the doping of Cu was adopted to suppress the Jahn-Teller effect of Mn3+ and to affect relevant structural parameters.  Multifunctions of the Cu2+ doping were studied.  It was found that the structure component ratio is varied with the Cu2+ doping amt.  Results demonstrated that Na+/vacancy rearrangement and phase transitions were suppressed during cycling without sacrificing the reversible capacity and enhanced electrochem. performances evidenced with 96 mAh/g retained after 250 cycles at 4 C and 85 mAh/g at 8 C.  Ex situ x-ray diffraction has demonstrated high reversibility of the Na0.6Mn0.9Cu0.1O2 cathode during Na+ extn./insertion processes and superior air stability that results in better storage properties.  This study reveals that the Cu2+ doping could be an effective strategy to tune the properties and related performances of Mn-based layer-tunnel hybrid cathode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrDlw2Tmt_qsbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhhWTE0wPz8Zw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unexpected effects of zirconium-doping in the high performance sodium manganese-based layer-tunnel cathode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qu, Jie; Sheng, Tian; Wu, Zhen-guo; Chen, Ting-ru; Chen, Hui; Yang, Zu-guang; Guo, Xiao-dong; Li, Jun-tao; Zhong, Ben-he; Dou, Xue-shi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">28</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13934-13942</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hybrid electrode materials, which could integrate the resp. advantages and overcome the drawbacks of each identical component, have caught vast attention and displayed promising applications.  Recently, manganese (Mn)-based layer-tunnel hybrid cathodes (NaxMnO2) have shown enhanced performance based on the amalgamation of high capacity (layer structure), excellent stability, and high rate capability (tunnel structure).  Ion-doping is usually carried out to det. the underlying performance.  Moreover, ion-doping would tune the component ratio and adjust the crystal structure at the same time, which may affect the balanced synergistic effect of the pristine sample.  With the help of d. functional theory (DFT), we predicted that zirconium ions (Zr4+) could fulfill an equal-tendency doping, which could almost maintain the original hybrid structure component ratio and focus on the crystal structure adjustment.  The Zr4+ doping effects were systematically investigated for both structure properties and sodium storage behavior.  The stronger bond energy of Zr-O and larger ionic radius of Zr4+ could weaken the charge order and significantly enhance cycling stability and rate performance.  The structure evolution and ion transportation kinetics were carefully tracked during the charge-discharge process.  The designed material, Na0.6Mn0.98Zr0.02O2, can deliver a high capacity of 81 mA h g-1 at 2 A g-1 with 75% retention after 1000 cycles.  Excellent full cell performance evidently proves the application potential.  This study may suggest a possible new scope for the design of high performance hybrid electrodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGri-QNwZPQow7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhhWTE0wPz8Zw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtFOktLzJ&amp;md5=c85c70e116db96ba382ccfbd2193fa8c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1142/S1793604713500124"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ni, J.-F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.-B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, L.-J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flux Synthesis of Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> Nanoribbons and Their Electrochemical Properties for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Funct.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Well-crystd. Na0.44MnO2 is readily synthesized via a facile NaCl-flux reaction at 850°C for 5 h.  The Na0.44MnO2 material exhibits a well-defined nanoribbon structure with dimension of 50-100 nm in thickness and 200-500 nm in width.  Electrochem. properties of as-prepd.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The aq. sodium-ion battery system is a safe and low-cost soln. for large-scale energy storage, because of the abundance of sodium and inexpensive aq. electrolytes.  Although several pos. electrode materials, for example, Na0.44MnO2, were proposed, few neg. electrode materials, for example, activated carbon and NaTi2(PO4)3, are available.  Here we show that Ti-substituted Na0.44MnO2 (Na0.44[Mn1-xTix]O2) with tunnel structure can be used as a neg. electrode material for aq. sodium-ion batteries.  This material exhibits superior cyclability even without the special treatment of oxygen removal from the aq. soln.  Atomic-scale characterizations based on spherical aberration-cor. electron microscopy and ab initio calcns. are utilized to accurately identify the Ti substitution sites and sodium storage mechanism.  Ti substitution tunes the charge ordering property and reaction pathway, significantly smoothing the discharge/charge profiles and lowering the storage voltage.  Both the fundamental understanding and practical demonstrations suggest that Na0.44[Mn1-xTix]O2 is a promising neg. electrode material for aq. sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGohCk2_kY_2DrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhhWTE0wPz8Zw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtF2lurrN&amp;md5=1e5e76f51babf6ca31b7d06baffc5277</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.7b00164"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alvarad, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Clement, R.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kodur, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tong, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Grey, C.-P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng, Y.-S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Exploring Oxygen Activity in the High Energy P2-Type Na<sub>0.78</sub>Ni<sub>0.23</sub>Mn<sub>0.69</sub>O<sub>2</sub> Cathode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Large-scale elec. energy storage is fundamental to the use of renewable energy.  Recently, research and development efforts on room-temp. sodium-ion batteries (NIBs) have been revitalized, as NIBs are considered promising, low-cost alternatives to the current Li-ion battery technol. for large-scale applications.  Herein, we introduce a novel layered oxide cathode material, Na0.78Ni0.23Mn0.69O2.  This new compd. provides a high reversible capacity of 138 mAh g-1 and an av. potential of 3.25 V vs Na+/Na with a single smooth voltage profile.  Its remarkable rate and cycling performances are attributed to the elimination of the P2-O2 phase transition upon cycling to 4.5 V.  The first charge process yields an abnormally excess capacity, which has yet to be obsd. in other P2 layered oxides.  Metal K-edge XANES results show that the major charge compensation at the metal site during Na-ion deintercalation is achieved via the oxidn. of nickel (Ni2+) ions, whereas, to a large extent, manganese (Mn) ions remain in their Mn4+ state.  Interestingly, electron energy loss spectroscopy (EELS) and soft x-ray absorption spectroscopy (sXAS) results reveal differences in electronic structures in the bulk and at the surface of electrochem. cycled particles.  At the surface, transition metal ions (TM ions) are in a lower valence state than in the bulk, and the O K-edge prepeak disappears.  On the basis of previous reports on related Li-excess LIB cathodes, it is proposed that part of the charge compensation mechanism during the first cycle takes place at the lattice oxygen site, resulting in a surface to bulk transition metal gradient.  We believe that by optimizing and controlling oxygen activity, Na layered oxide materials with higher capacities can be designed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqY1N7fQiMowbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhhWTE0wPz8Zw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXjvVOntrs%253D&amp;md5=0639ce6b577c8672161733590246a4ad</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA10589G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Unveilingthe Role of Co in Improving the High-Rate Capability and Cycling Performanceof Layered Na<sub>0.7</sub>Mn<sub>0.7</sub>Ni<sub>0.3–x</sub>Co<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">New insights into designing high-rate performance cathode materials for sodium ion batteries by enlarging the slab-spacing of the Na-ion diffusion layer</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zheng-Yao; Gao, Rui; Zhang, Jicheng; Zhang, Xiuling; Hu, Zhongbo; Liu, Xiangfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, the design and synthesis of high performance cathode materials for sodium ion batteries have attracted great interest.  In this study, a novel strategy is proposed to design high-rate performance cathode materials for sodium ion batteries through enlarging the d-spacing of the Na-ion diffusion layer.  More importantly, some new insights into the expansion mechanism of the interplanar spacing for Na0.67Mn0.8Ni0.1Mg0.1O2 induced by Ni and Mg co-doping and the resulting high-rate capability have been presented for the first time.  It was found that Mg and Ni co-doping leads to the shortening of the TM-O (TM = transition metal) bond lengths and the shrinkage of the TMO6 octahedrons, which might be largely responsible for the expansion of the interplanar spacing of the Na-ion diffusion layer.  In comparison with Na0.67Mn0.8Ni0.2O2 and Na0.67Mn0.8Mg0.2O2, Mg and Ni co-doped Na0.67Mn0.8Ni0.1Mg0.1O2 has a higher Na-ion diffusion coeff. and can deliver around 160, 145, 133 and 124 mA h g-1 at 24, 48, 120 and 240 mA g-1, resp.  In particular, at the high current densities of 480 (2C), 1200 (5C) and 1920 mA g-1 (8C), MMN can still offer reversible capacities of 110, 66 and 37 mA h g-1, resp.  In addn., the cycling stability has also been enhanced via Mg and Ni co-doping at the same time, which means that Mg and Ni co-doping also has a pos. effect on the stability of the layered structure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr44MtsleAxP7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgCoh-6tUMPNA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improving the Performance of Layered Oxide Cathode Materials with Football-Like Hierarchical Structure for Na-Ion Batteries by Incorporating Mg2+ into Vacancies in Na-Ion Layers</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zheng-Yao; Wang, Huibo; Chen, Dongfeng; Sun, Kai; Yang, Wenyun; Yang, Jinbo; Liu, Xiangfeng; Han, Songbai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemSusChem</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The development of advanced cathode materials is still a great interest for sodium-ion batteries.  The feasible commercialization of sodium-ion batteries relies on the design and exploitation of suitable electrode materials.  This study offers a new insight into material design to exploit high-performance P2-type cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  The incorporation of Mg2+ into intrinsic Na+ vacancies in Na-ion layers can lead to a high-performance P2-type cathode material for sodium-ion batteries.  The materials prepd. by the copptn. approach show a well-defined morphol. of secondary football-like hierarchical structures.  Neutron power diffraction and refinement results demonstrate that the incorporation of Mg2+ into intrinsic vacancies can enlarge the space for Na-ion diffusion, which can increase the d-spacing of the (0 0 2) peak and the size of slabs but reduce the chem. bond length to result in an enhanced rate capability and cycling stability.  The incorporation of Mg2+ into available vacancies and a unique morphol. make Na0.7Mg0.05Mn0.8Ni0.1Co0.1O2 a promising cathode, which can be charged and discharged at an ultra-high c.d. of 2000 mA g-1 with an excellent specific capacity of 60 mAh g-1.  This work provides a new insight into the design of electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrLYEKQOEAqBLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgCoh-6tUMPNA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXjvVyjs7s%253D&amp;md5=5de2425ed167a4499fe8edf01b32ec86</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-018-07646-4"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Noh, G.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Manganese based layered oxides with modulated electronic and thermodynamic properties for sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>Nat.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Manganese based layered oxides with modulated electronic and thermodynamic properties for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; Kim, Duho; Hu, Zhe; Park, Mihui; Noh, Gahee; Yang, Yujeong; Zhang, Jing; Lau, Vincent Wing-hei; Chou, Shu-Lei; Cho, Maenghyo; Choi, Si-Young; Kang, Yong-Mook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Manganese based layered oxides have received increasing attention as cathode materials for sodium ion batteries due to their high theor. capacities and good sodium ion conductivities.  However, the Jahn-Teller distortion arising from the manganese (III) centers destabilizes the host structure and deteriorates the cycling life.  Herein, we report that zinc-doped Na0.833[Li0.25Mn0.75]O2 can not only suppress the Jahn-Teller effect but also reduce the inherent phase sepns.  The redn. of manganese (III) amt. in the zinc-doped sample, as predicted by first-principles calcns., has been confirmed by its high binding energies and the reduced octahedral structural variations.  In the viewpoint of thermodn., the zinc-doped sample has lower formation energy, more stable ground states, and fewer spinodal decompn. regions than those of the undoped sample, all of which make it charge or discharge without any phase transition.  Hence, the zinc-doped sample shows superior cycling performance, demonstrating that zinc doping is an effective strategy for developing high-performance layered cathode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp_U8-D0B6GN7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgCoh-6tUMPNA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXmvFSrt7k%253D&amp;md5=01c20eca7a25e8b9b0ec1e404bff56a3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA06551A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, T.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Simultaneous MgO coating and Mg doping of Na[Ni0.5Mn0.5]O2 cathode: facile and customizable approach to high-voltage sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Yu, Tae-Yeon; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, we report substantially improved high-voltage stability of Na[Ni0.5Mn0.5]O2 as a cathode material due to a surface MgO coating and bulk Mg doping for high-voltage sodium-ion batteries, for the first time.  The MgO coating layer effectively suppressed the unfavorable side reactions during cycling while the partial Mg doping into the bulk Ni sites improved the structural stability by moderating the extent of the irreversible multiphase transformation.  As a result, the combination of a MgO coating with Mg doping provides enhanced electrochem. performance and structural stability of Na[Ni0.5Mn0.5]O2 within the voltage range of 2.0-4.2 V.  The material demonstrated a high specific capacity of 167 mA h g-1 at a 0.1C and excellent cycling stability and rate capability with 60% capacity retention at 10C (vs. the initial capacity at 0.1C).  The practical acceptability of the simultaneous MgO coating and Mg doping of the Na[Ni0.5Mn0.5]O2 cathode was obviously verified using scaled-up pouch-type full cells with hard carbon anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp6fA3M7OKwmLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgCoh-6tUMPNA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhsFKqtrrP&amp;md5=6e6132d702487b54d5dd61a9f3d07061</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1039/C7EE00566K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ortiz

                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High performance manganese-based layered oxide cathodes: overcoming the challenges of sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ortiz-Vitoriano, Nagore; Drewett, Nicholas E.; Gonzalo, Elena; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1051-1074</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Currently, there is increasing interest in developing 'beyond lithium' battery technologies to augment, or in certain situations replace, lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  Room temp. sodium ion batteries (NIBs) offer an attractive combination of low cost and plentiful constituents and a wide range of phases, structures and stoichiometries available for optimization.  Sodium layered oxides are considered to be promising candidates as cathode materials, due to their flexibility and versatility, as well as their intrinsically fast structural diffusion of Na ions which leads to enhanced rate capability.  In particular, sodium manganese based layered oxides (generally NaxMn1-y-zMyTMzO2, where TM represents one or more transition metals, and M consists of one or more non-transition metals) are a key family of materials, in part due to the relatively low cost and environmentally friendly nature of the manganese, and consequently are worthy of a detailed investigation.  Examn. of these systems, particularly in terms of stoichiometry and phase, has shown that significant advances have been made recently, both in terms of understanding the mechanisms behind electrochem. performance, and in terms of refining these to produce improved materials.  The goal of this review is to present the current developments in sodium manganese based layered oxides (particularly with respect to electrochem. performance, phys. properties and manganese content), to discuss the current state of this field of research and to draw conclusions regarding where future investigations may be most fruitfully directed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpE3sm-UBXaRLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgCoh-6tUMPNA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">P2-Type NaxCu0.15Ni0.20Mn0.65O2 Cathodes with High Voltage for High-Power and Long-Life Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kang, Wenpei; Yu, Denis Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Cu-Ni-Mn-based ternary P2-type NaxCu0.15Ni0.20Mn0.65O2 (x = 0.50, 0.67, 0.75) cathodes for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) were synthesized by a co-pptn. method.  Na content plays a key role on the structure, morphol., and the charge-discharge performances of these materials.  For x = 0.67 and 0.75, superstructure from Na+-vacancy ordering is obsd., while it is absent in the x = 0.50 sample.  Despite the same synthesis conditions, materials with x = 0.67 and 0.75 show smaller particle sizes compared to that of the x = 0.50 sample.  Redox potentials of the materials differ significantly even though they have the same transition metal ratios.  These differences are attributed to the changes in local structures of the as-prepd. materials arising from the different amt. of Na and possibly O in the lattice.  Materials with x = 0.67 and 0.75 show excellent rate performance and cycle stability when tested as cathode material of SIBs.  Av. discharge potential is ≤ 3.41 V vs. Na-Na+ with capacity of 87 mAh g-1 at 20 mA g-1.  Excellent capacity and cycle stability are maintained even when they are tested with higher current rates.  For instance, a capacity of 62.3 mAh g-1 was obtained from the x = 0.67 sample at 1000 mA g-1 after 1000 cycles between 3.0 and 4.2 V without any decrease in capacity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpj-2V9UTqtcLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhVjT_V471LUg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslOhsr7L&amp;md5=8099b5ff7c7982d331d667068ea2bf41</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.7b02772"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kumakura, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tahara, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sato, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">P’2-Na<sub>2/3</sub>Mn<sub>0.9</sub>Me<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (Me = Mg, Ti, Co, Ni, Cu, and Zn): Correlation Between Orthorhombic Distortion and Electrochemical Property</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">P'2-Na2/3Mn0.9Me0.1O2 (Me = Mg, Ti, Co, Ni, Cu, and Zn): Correlation between Orthorhombic Distortion and Electrochemical Property</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kumakura, Shinichi; Tahara, Yoshiyuki; Sato, Syuhei; Kubota, Kei; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Single-phase samples of differently distorted P'2-Na2/3Mn0.9Me0.1O2 (Me = Mg, Ti, Co, Ni, Cu, and Zn) were synthesized by a conventional solid-state reaction.  Cooperative Jahn-Teller distortion, which causes an orthorhombic lattice from a distortion-free hexagonal lattice, proportionally increases with increase in the concn. of Jahn-Teller ions of Mn III and Cu II in P'2-Na2/3Mn0.9Me0.1O2.  All of samples deliver initial reversible capacity approaching 230 mAh g-1 in nonaq. Na cells.  The redox potential of Mn(III/IV) with Na extn. is highly correlated with degree of the distortion.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">P2-type Nax[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2 made from earth-abundant elements for rechargeable Na batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Kajiyama, Masataka; Iwatate, Junichi; Nishikawa, Heisuke; Hitomi, Shuji; Okuyama, Ryoichi; Usui, Ryo; Yamada, Yasuhiro; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable Li batteries have risen to prominence as key devices for green and sustainable energy development.  Mn- and Fe-based cathode materials, such as LiMn2O4 and LiFePO4, are used in large-scale batteries for elec. vehicles.  Mn and Fe are abundant elements in the Earth's crust, but Li is not.  In contrast to Li, Na is an attractive charge carrier from elemental abundance.  Recently, some layered materials, where Na can be electrochem. and reversibly extd./inserted, have been reported.  However, their reversible capacity is typically limited to 100 mA-h/g.  Herein, the authors report a new electrode material, P2-Na2/3[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2, that delivers 190 mA-h/g of reversible capacity in Na cells with the electrochem. active Fe3+/Fe4+ redox.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Multiangular Rod-Shaped Na0.44MnO2 as Cathode Materials with High Rate and Long Life for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Qiannan; Hu, Zhe; Chen, Mingzhe; Gu, Qinfen; Dou, Yuhai; Sun, Ziqi; Chou, Shulei; Dou, Shi Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
